   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Herodotus
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>

    </div>

          <img alt="Herodotos Met 91.8.jpg" data-file-height="3924" data-file-width="2616" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Herodotos_Met_91.8.jpg/220px-Herodotos_Met_91.8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Herodotos_Met_91.8.jpg/330px-Herodotos_Met_91.8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Herodotos_Met_91.8.jpg/440px-Herodotos_Met_91.8.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
         </a>

         <br/>
         <span class="deathplace">

          </a>
          ,
          <a href="/wiki/Calabria" title="Calabria">

          </a>
          or

           Pella
          </a>
          ,

       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <b>
        Herodotus
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'h' in 'hi'">
            h
           </span>
           <span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">
            ɪ
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'r' in 'rye'">
            r
           </span>
           <span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">
            ɒ
           </span>
           <span title="'d' in 'dye'">
            d
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ;
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" title="Ancient Greek language">
        Ancient Greek
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="grc">
        Ἡρόδοτος
       </span>
       ,
       <i>
        Hêródotos
       </i>
       ,
       <small>
        <a href="/wiki/Attic_Greek" title="Attic Greek">
         Attic Greek
        </a>
        pronunciation:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Greek" title="Help:IPA/Greek">
         [hɛː.ró.do.tos]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) was a
       <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">
        Greek
       </a>
       historian who was born in
       <a href="/wiki/Halicarnassus" title="Halicarnassus">
        Halicarnassus
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">
        Persian Empire
       </a>
       (modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Bodrum" title="Bodrum">
        Bodrum
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
        Turkey
       </a>
       ) and lived in the fifth century BC (
       <abbr title="circa">
        c.
       </abbr>
       484–c. 425 BC), a contemporary of
       <a href="/wiki/Thucydides" title="Thucydides">
        Thucydides
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Socrates" title="Socrates">
        Socrates
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Euripides" title="Euripides">
        Euripides
       </a>
       . He is often referred to as "The Father of History", a title first conferred by
       <a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">
        Cicero
       </a>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       he was the first historian known to have broken from
       <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">
        Homeric
       </a>
       tradition to treat historical subjects as a method of investigation—specifically, by collecting his materials systematically and critically, and then arranging them into a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historiographic" title="Historiographic">
        historiographic
       </a>
       narrative.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Histories_(Herodotus)" title="Histories (Herodotus)">
         The Histories
        </a>
       </i>
       is the only work which he is known to have produced, a record of his "inquiry" (
       <span lang="grc" title="Ancient Greek language text">
        ἱστορία
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/History#Etymology" title="History">
        <i>
         historía
        </i>
       </a>
       ) on the origins of the
       <a href="/wiki/Greco-Persian_Wars" title="Greco-Persian Wars">
        Greco-Persian Wars
       </a>
       ; it primarily deals with the lives of
       <a href="/wiki/Croesus" title="Croesus">
        Croesus
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cyrus_the_Great" title="Cyrus the Great">
        Cyrus
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cambyses_II" title="Cambyses II">
        Cambyses
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bardiya" title="Bardiya">
        Smerdis
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Darius_I" title="Darius I">
        Darius
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Xerxes_I" title="Xerxes I">
        Xerxes
       </a>
       and the battles of
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Marathon" title="Battle of Marathon">
        Marathon
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Thermopylae" title="Battle of Thermopylae">
        Thermopylae
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Artemisium" title="Battle of Artemisium">
        Artemisium
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Salamis" title="Battle of Salamis">
        Salamis
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plataea" title="Battle of Plataea">
        Plataea
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Mycale" title="Battle of Mycale">
        Mycale
       </a>
       ; however, its many cultural,
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnography" title="Ethnography">
        ethnographical
       </a>
       , geographical,
       <a href="/wiki/Historiography" title="Historiography">
        historiographical
       </a>
       , and other digressions form a defining and essential part of the
       <i>
        Histories
       </i>
       and contain a wealth of information. Some of his stories are fanciful and others inaccurate, yet he states that he is reporting only what he was told; a sizable portion of the information he provided was later confirmed by historians and archaeologists.
      </p>
      <p>
       Despite Herodotus's historical significance, little is known of his personal life.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18">
         <a href="#See_also">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           6
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           See also
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19">
         <a href="#Critical_editions">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           7
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Critical editions
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20">
         <a href="#Translations">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           8
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Translations
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21">
         <a href="#Notes">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           9
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Notes
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22">
         <a href="#References">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           10
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           References
          </span>
         </a>
         <ul>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23">
           <a href="#Sources">
            <span class="tocnumber">
             10.1
            </span>

            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24">
         <a href="#Further_reading">
          <span class="tocnumber">

          </span>

          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-25">
